<div id="review_2026615551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2026615551" />
    <a title="Samir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52081294-samir"><img alt="Samir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588945560p2/52081294.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2026615551?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samir" href="/user/show/52081294-samir">Samir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2026615551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7260107526398944424">It is always a great feeling to start the last book of the trilogy, especially if you loved the previous books. Excitement, curiosity, eagerness, all mixed up in a huge ball of emotions. The ending of the <i>Royal Assassin</i> was a game changer and it lifted my expectations for this book in such way that I couldn’t wait to find out what will happen next with Fitz and his companions and what fate will befall the Six Duchies.<br/><br/>Writing this review wasn’t an easy task. Not because I was struggling to channe</span>
  <span id="freeText7260107526398944424" style="display:none">It is always a great feeling to start the last book of the trilogy, especially if you loved the previous books. Excitement, curiosity, eagerness, all mixed up in a huge ball of emotions. The ending of the <i>Royal Assassin</i> was a game changer and it lifted my expectations for this book in such way that I couldn’t wait to find out what will happen next with Fitz and his companions and what fate will befall the Six Duchies.<br /><br />Writing this review wasn’t an easy task. Not because I was struggling to channel my thoughts and find the proper words but because I couldn’t really mention the important and interesting things that happened. If I did, this review would have been a few sentences long and filled with spoilers. Unfortunately, this only means that not many things of importance happened and that was my biggest problem with this book and it affected my rating.<br /><br />I already mentioned the ending of the previous book. Based on those events, I imagined, or to be honest, hoped, that this book would be an epic tale of revenge and the quest of our main hero would be filled with interesting and action packed encounters with the Forged, the Red Ships and Regal’s soldiers and members of his coterie. Sadly, those encounters were rare and the biggest part of Fitz’s quest was traveling. Long travels usually mean slow pace and I usually don’t mind slow pace in books when it has a purpose of introducing us with the characters and the plot but that is generally more common in the first or middle book of the series, not the last one where we expect things to pick up and all those plot threads to resolve. This book really suffered from it and I dare say that it suffered from that infamous “middle book syndrome” even though it wasn’t a middle book however strange or stupid this may sound to you. That feeling I mentioned in the beginning of this review was depleted as I kept on reading. This felt like I was reading a travel log of a tea enthusiast. Fitz would travel, gather some herbs in the process, there was a vast description of his surroundings, he would meet some people here and there and then he would make some tea. And almost every woman he met wanted to sleep with him. I don’t know what kind of herb is elfbark but if someone knows where to find it, please let me know. This was so boring and it kept me putting this book down a lot and starting something else. Maybe this won’t bother you much but it made finishing this book a lot harder for me and it left me wondering was it all really that necessary. What I really want to say is that this book could have been much shorter and the “less is more principle” could be applied here.<br /> <br />The only thing that kept me going was the hope that the pace will pick up and soar even, leaving me catching for my breath as the adrenaline rushed through my body because of the immense action and sadly, it never did. When Fitz finally found Verity nothing groundbreaking happened and I was a bit disappointed.<br /><br />Before I convey my final thoughts, I have to mention the side characters. Other than the wolf Nighteyes, with whom I fell in love with from the first moment I met him and who will remain as one my favorite fantasy characters ever, I was left with the impression that they are a bunch of assholes. No matter what Fitz did and no matter how big the sacrifices he had to make to achieve the goals of others, it was never enough for them and they always demanded more of him and made him feel like crap. No wonder he was depressed and miserable all the time which made loving him as a character hard but I was able to connect with him anyway because I’ve had similar experience with people.<br /> <br />The grand finale was underwhelming. I expected a grand battle but instead I got a “Veni, vidi, vici” recap of things. After enduring the prolonged build up, the ending sequence felt a bit rushed and everything was so anticlimatic and left me apathetic.<br /><br />The writing was beautiful and I’m sure Hobb’s prose had an impact on many writers of epic fantasy, but sometimes, I need something more. <i>Assassin’s Quest</i> failed to meet my expectations and it fell short in delivering the thrilling conclusion I was hoping for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7260107526398944424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_159330830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159330830" />
    <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship"><img alt="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325201543p2/5229326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159330830?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship">Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553565690" href="/book/show/45112.Assassin_s_Quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159330830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15160187103259549742">I very rarely give only one star; it feels melodramatic, especially since I gave Royal Assassin five. But after the quality of the first two books in this trilogy, I was shocked and appalled by this one--and, what's worse, I was bored. <br/><br/>In this book, Fitz leaves Buckkeep and all of the other characters we've come to know and love over the first two books. He spends most of the 760-page book hiking across the continent, much of it alone, much of the rest with random throwaway characters who appear</span>
  <span id="freeText15160187103259549742" style="display:none">I very rarely give only one star; it feels melodramatic, especially since I gave Royal Assassin five. But after the quality of the first two books in this trilogy, I was shocked and appalled by this one--and, what's worse, I was bored. <br /><br />In this book, Fitz leaves Buckkeep and all of the other characters we've come to know and love over the first two books. He spends most of the 760-page book hiking across the continent, much of it alone, much of the rest with random throwaway characters who appear for the first time in this book (many of whom disappear after a couple chapters and proceed to have no more impact on the plot). It all feels like filler. When he finally meets up with other major characters, there's more walking, more filler... what happened to all the passion and intrigue of the first two books? It's hard to put my finger on what went wrong here. It feels as if the author just stopped caring. Even the writing became repetitive. <br /><br />Then there's the end. It's just awful. Hobb leaves all the antagonists that have been wreaking havoc throughout the trilogy to be dealt with in the last 30 pages or so; inevitably, it's rushed. Not only that, it happens off-screen, in narrative summary. You thought after all this pain you'd actually get to see a final battle with the Red Ships, or Fitz assassinating Regal? Nope. The ending itself is decidedly bittersweet, but after this slog I no longer cared about the characters I'd been so emotionally attached to for the first two books, so it didn't really bother me. <br /><br />I've tried to find some redeeming quality here, but honestly thought the book was hideous, and it definitely brings down my opinion of the trilogy. It's a shame because the first two books were so good... if only this had been a duology. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15160187103259549742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1032597522" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1032597522" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408028716p2/17295220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1032597522?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553565690" href="/book/show/45112.Assassin_s_Quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295220-alexa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032597522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer120579888736955433"><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900632132' rel='nofollow noopener'>Markus</a></b><br/><br/>I have a lot of friends who love Hobb's series, so I'm going to assume the problem here is one of compatibility: <b>this book and I, we're just not compatible. </b><br/><br/>I tend to like plot driven books, well developed villains, and I don't want a Gary Stu protagonist, but I do want my hero to be heroic. To win from time to time. It's the main character and I'm following his story, of course I'm going to root for him!<br/><br/>Sadly this book followed a pattern I didn't like: <br/><br/><i>1. Fitz would do som</i></span>
  <span id="freeText120579888736955433" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900632132" rel="nofollow noopener">Markus</a></b><br /><br />I have a lot of friends who love Hobb's series, so I'm going to assume the problem here is one of compatibility: <b>this book and I, we're just not compatible. </b><br /><br />I tend to like plot driven books, well developed villains, and I don't want a Gary Stu protagonist, but I do want my hero to be heroic. To win from time to time. It's the main character and I'm following his story, of course I'm going to root for him!<br /><br />Sadly this book followed a pattern I didn't like: <br /><br /><i>1. Fitz would do something wrong, often because he didn't know better. <br />2. Someone more knowledgeable would scold Fitz for being ignorant, but would not explain stuff.<br />3. Since Fitz still doesn't know anything, he'd do something wrong again. <br />Rinse and repeat. </i><br /><br />This happened at least 5 times during the book, twice Fitz was betrayed, a few times Fitz was just an idiot and did something when he knew better, and some times things simply went wrong. <br /><br />And that was the plot of the book. By the end I was completely tired of everything going wrong again, and again, and again. <br /><br />And Regal, our villain. I was so confused by him. I kept feeling like I had two very different villains. Sometimes he'd be portrayed as nothing more than a spoiled child turned into a terrible prince; yet sometimes he'd have enough cunning to place spies, foul Fitz's plots and devise strategies. <br /><br />Who's the real Regal then? The cunning evil one? Or the spoiled brat who drinks too much and smokes too much and should by all accounts be too drugged to hatch up any kind of plan? There was a complete mix up in the characterization here that made my head hurt more than once. <br /><br />And then we get a completely disappointing ending. We don't even get to see the battle, it's narrated in an almost offhanded way. Like the threat from the Red Ships was nothing more than a red herring. A plot device conveniently set to get the plot moving, but of no consequence after all. <br /><br />Sadly, I can't say I liked this book and I don't think I'll be reading anything else in the series. :(</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1876208290" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1876208290" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45400990-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573825853p2/45400990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1876208290?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/45400990-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45400990-laura?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1876208290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer287815718780474969">I must confess I fell in love - with a wolf and a fool, a queen and her dragon and a little boy who, stumbling through life, falling and blundering at every step, grew into a better, wiser man. I fell in love with the world Robin Hobb created in these pages. Assassin's Quest was for me even better than the previous 2 books of Farseer. And the trilogy as a whole took a place of honour on my "all time favourites" shelf.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1996269708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996269708" />
    <a title="Sean Gibson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson"><img alt="Sean Gibson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416866667p2/20955173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1996269708?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Gibson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Gibson" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson">Sean Gibson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996269708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4310839338357868820">Having now completed the Farseer trilogy, I’ve identified three major characteristics of Hobbs’ novels: <br/><br/>1. The writing is beautiful—poetic yet practical, powerful yet prosaic; perfectly suited to the world and story<br/>2. Considerable time is spent within the mind of a beleaguered narrator, and much of the action takes place in a metaphysical plane <br/>3. Things…move…very…sssslllloooowwwwllllyyyy<br/><br/>(To be fair, all of the above is true of my own books, except for #1 and #2.)<br/><br/>The concluding volume of the ser</span>
  <span id="freeText4310839338357868820" style="display:none">Having now completed the Farseer trilogy, I’ve identified three major characteristics of Hobbs’ novels: <br /><br />1. The writing is beautiful—poetic yet practical, powerful yet prosaic; perfectly suited to the world and story<br />2. Considerable time is spent within the mind of a beleaguered narrator, and much of the action takes place in a metaphysical plane <br />3. Things…move…very…sssslllloooowwwwllllyyyy<br /><br />(To be fair, all of the above is true of my own books, except for #1 and #2.)<br /><br />The concluding volume of the series is perhaps its most ponderous, and the weight of time drags on it like seaweed wrapped around your ankle when you’re swimming and trying to escape the spongy muck at the bottom of the lake. No matter how quickly you thrash about, no matter how hard you push, you just can’t move much faster. <br /><br />That’s not to say that it’s not an entertaining tale, mind you—see point #1 above, and there are some particularly interesting revelations about the connection between FitzEyore* and the Fool that I won’t spoil here (along similar lines, the Deus ex Machina-esque appearance of a certain fantasy creature at the book’s end is pretty exciting). But, I can’t help but feel that there’s a great story trapped within this good one, hindered from breaking free of the muck only for lack of a sharp (and ruthless) editor’s pencil. <br /><br />On balance, the trilogy itself is a worthwhile read and a very well developed example of world building; I just wish that the meandering pace of the first volume hadn’t presaged the glacial pace of its successors.<br /><br />In recognition of the overall quality of the writing, and because I’m feeling saucy (then again, when am I NOT feeling saucy, given that it’s virtually impossible for me to eat anything without spilling sauce on myself, which is true even when I’m eating something that doesn’t have any sauce, which is quite a feat of comestidigitation, I can tell you, and you can take that to the bank, or maybe just to the internet if, like me, you just do mobile banking and, like me, choose to no longer recognize “Internet” as a proper noun), we’ll round up from 3.5 stars. <br /><br />*Not his actual name, but it might as well be. Man. That guy is just a bad luck magnet. He is to terrible things happening to him as I am to tripping over nothing in particular and then breaking into a light jog in order to pretend that was my intention all along.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4310839338357868820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1336458324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1336458324" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1336458324?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553565690" href="/book/show/45112.Assassin_s_Quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1336458324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17399359698399961658"><i>“When you try your best but you don't succeed<br/>When you get what you want but not what you need<br/>When you feel so tired but you can't sleep<br/>Stuck in reverse”</i><br/> - Coldplay<br/><br/>There is a kind of trope in epic fantasy where the Chosen One gets angry at being chosen, at what he has to sacrifice for the global benefit, and what a terrible time he is having. Frodo, Harry Potter etc. all go through this “woe is me” phase. FitzChivalry, the protagonist of this “Farseer Trilogy” does <i>a lot</i> of that in this final vol</span>
  <span id="freeText17399359698399961658" style="display:none"><i>“When you try your best but you don't succeed<br>When you get what you want but not what you need<br>When you feel so tired but you can't sleep<br>Stuck in reverse”</i><br> - Coldplay<br><br>There is a kind of trope in epic fantasy where the Chosen One gets angry at being chosen, at what he has to sacrifice for the global benefit, and what a terrible time he is having. Frodo, Harry Potter etc. all go through this “woe is me” phase. FitzChivalry, the protagonist of this “Farseer Trilogy” does <i>a lot</i> of that in this final volume of the trilogy. To quote Prince (formerly “The artist formerly known as Prince”): “Shut up already, damn!” Perhaps a bit of Coldplay would have fixed him.<br><br>So! The final volume of The Farseer Trilogy – hurrah! I love reading final volumes of trilogies, it is an accomplishment of sorts (that no one but you cares about) and it also gives you a sense of closure. Of course, the series continue with new trilogies, but there is no cliffhanger to spoil your day. <i>Assassin's Quest</i> of course, moves right along from the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68487.Royal_Assassin__Farseer_Trilogy___2_" title="Royal Assassin (Farseer Trilogy, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener"> Royal Assassin</a> where our hero Fitz was apparently beaten and tortured to death by the dastardly Prince Regal. Of course having much more protagonistic work to do he did not die but stuffed his soul into Nighteyes the wolf to be downloaded and restored into his body when the bad guys are not around. After recovering (about 80%) from his wounds and whining at his two best friends and mentors so hard they pack up and leave him, he goes off on the eponymous quest to find the missing Prince Verity who went off to a remote mountain range to find the legendary Elderlings to aid the people of his Kingdom. The plot sounds silly when I recount it but it actually is a damn fine story with oodles of plots, intrigue, excitement, characters and emo bits.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470209870i/19900581._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Fitz looking more mature in this older edition's cover<br><br>What I particularly like about this series is how the fantastical element is implemented (I dislike the term “magic system”, it sounds inappropriately techy for fantasy). Anyway, much of the magic in this series resemble that old Golden Age Sci-Fi chestnut “psi powers”, telepathy, premonition, psychic attacks, astral projection and whatnot; of course Robin Hobb has her own terms for these things. This helps to boost the believability of the series' universe for me. I am not a big fan of spells and incantations in epic fantasy, they just seem too Cinderella for my taste. Having said that things become much <i>much</i> more magical toward the end of the book but by then I was already so deep into the book I did not really care.<br><br>There is an elegance to Ms. Hobb’s writing that I tend to associate with female authors. However, she is also adept at depicting some very badass fight scenes. The characters are skillfully developed and quite vivid. The Fool continues to be the most unique and interesting characters in the series, though he is much less enigmatic here than he was in previous volumes. Nighteyes the wolf is much improved from his appearances in the first two books when he was basically just an annoying pup. In <i>Assassin's Quest</i> he is clever, resourceful, loyal and generally very lovable. My only gripe with the characterization is the central character FitzChivalry. For practically the entire book he makes the same mistakes over and over and complains incessantly. I don’t remember him being this whiny in the previous books. Ms. Hobb’s penchant for angst and melodrama also bogs the narrative down from time to time and made the book longer than it needs to be (757 pages).<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470209870i/19900582._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>2016's <a href="http://subterraneanpress.com/store/product_detail/the_farseer_trilogy" rel="nofollow noopener">expensive special edition</a>, cover art by John Howe.<br><br>Still, <i>Assassin's Quest</i> is a damn good read, mostly well paced and has a rousing climax. If you are looking for a fantasy series to read do pick up the first volume <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice__Farseer_Trilogy___1_" title="Assassin's Apprentice (Farseer Trilogy, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener"> Assassin's Apprentice</a> which Amazon has <s>kindly</s> made available at a very low price to entrap you into Hobb addiction, it kinda works. I am not sure I am on board for the subsequent trilogies of this series, they require a lot of time commitment and I feel the first trilogy is nice and complete by itself. Fitz should just acquire a comfy chair, kick back, smoke a pipe and start a stamp collection or something. I am glad I have read this trilogy, though, it’s pretty damn awesome.<br><a href="http://www.john-howe.com/portfolio/gallery/data/media/20/big/RoyalAssassin-port.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470210109i/19900595._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br>The Stone Dragon scene by John Howe (click to embiggen).</span>
  <a data-text-id="17399359698399961658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2071381549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2071381549" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2071381549?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/31367113-assassin-s-quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2071381549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9291538053306144577">What was that? I can't believe it ended this miserably, it would have been better if he died, I hate this book with passion, 900+ pages for this? 😠<br/><br/>It took me nearly three months to finish this book, I started Dec, 27th and finished on March, 20th, I read a total number of 26 books between the time it took for me to finish this book, it was not because it was overly long, it was just too frustrating and I refused to dnf it, they are like so many reasons why I loathe this book, its the worst endin</span>
  <span id="freeText9291538053306144577" style="display:none">What was that? I can't believe it ended this miserably, it would have been better if he died, I hate this book with passion, 900+ pages for this? 😠<br /><br />It took me nearly three months to finish this book, I started Dec, 27th and finished on March, 20th, I read a total number of 26 books between the time it took for me to finish this book, it was not because it was overly long, it was just too frustrating and I refused to dnf it, they are like so many reasons why I loathe this book, its the worst ending to a series that I've read in my life. What annoyed me most about this book is that it has so much potential to have been good, if only the author have made it half its size and ended it well.<br /><br /><u>World building and Writing</u><br />In the previous books I really enjoyed this parts of the book but here Miss Hobb ruined that, the world building is still okay but the unneccessary explicit descriptions of things that are not important made it boring and annoying, not to mention the internal monologue, it was so frustrating, the dialogues were still great but was very few.<br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br />My favourite is still FitzChilvary, his life is just filled with sacrifice, misery and trauma. He was almost never happy, Nighteyes and The Fool tried but he is so depressesd, its a wonder he is not even suicidal, okay he is a bit, His family are the worst ever, it still surprises how he still moves on with his life, well he is stronger than a lot of people and he also has a big heart.<br /><br />Verity disappointed me here, he asked too mich of Fitz, I know he loves him and all but it still doesn't change the fact, I know he'll do the same himself, but he has a choice and Fitz doesn't, I hate when he doesn't give Fitz a chance to choose.<br /><br />Same goes for Kettricken, Chade and Burrick, how could they do that to him.<br /><br />Molly don't deserve Fitz, I know he kept secrets and all but when he told her in the previous book, she believed he was lying, she even still thinks he lied to her despite all that has happened and the secret she kept from him, she choose for him just like the others.<br /><br />Starling tried but just like the Fool said she did it for a song and position, I like that they became friends but the foundation was rocky.<br /><br />Only the Fool and Nighteyes were there for him, and never asked too much of him, they instead sacrificed for him which is the true meaning of friendship.<br /><br /><u>Plot</u><br />The book started just where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25300956.Royal_Assassin__Farseer_Trilogy___2_" title="Royal Assassin (Farseer Trilogy, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Royal Assassin</a> ended, with Fitz trying to adjust to his life after the ordeal, those first few pages were amazing then everything went downhill, it was like Miss Hobb wanted to torture us, all that happened for the next 400 or so pages was Fitz travelling with Nighteyes and for the most part alone and brooding and trying not to get himself killed, all the females he met suddenly want to have sex with him, I kid you not. I know Fitz is handsome and all but he admitted that after that ordeal in the previous book and him been just on a meat diet he looled like crap, sometimes people thought he was a begger, so how is it that they still want to have sex with him?<br /><br />After that annoying section of the book with just Fitz and his thoughts, he finally had company, The Fool changed things for the better and other fun characters too, but that again was ruined by Miss Hobb with that horrendous ending, I refuse to accept that as the ending to this series, things worked out for everyone except Fitz, would it have killed her to make him a tiny bit happy?<br /><br />To make matters worse, everyone was happy at his expense, his sacrifice made it worthwhile and it hurts that none of them even thought of him, Am sure none will do that for him, they just kept taking from him without thinking of what he was loosing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9291538053306144577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3417324170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3417324170" />
    <a title="Jade Ratley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57460119-jade-ratley"><img alt="Jade Ratley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594472805p2/57460119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3417324170?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jade Ratley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jade Ratley" href="/user/show/57460119-jade-ratley">Jade Ratley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007562275" href="/book/show/22016392-assassin-s-quest">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3417324170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4685717426354352245">7.00 in CAWPILE, so only just scaped a 4 star rating.<br/><br/>Although 4 stars is not a bad rating in anyone's mind, I must say I was disappointed by this book. It did not live up to the expectations I had of it in my mind. The only factor bringing the rating of this book up on CAWPILE is Characters, which I have consistently rated 9/10 as the characters are so well crafted. The Atmosphere, Writing, Logic and Enjoyment all came out at a 7 this time, so again not bad, but not fantastic. Plot and Intrigue </span>
  <span id="freeText4685717426354352245" style="display:none">7.00 in CAWPILE, so only just scaped a 4 star rating.<br /><br />Although 4 stars is not a bad rating in anyone's mind, I must say I was disappointed by this book. It did not live up to the expectations I had of it in my mind. The only factor bringing the rating of this book up on CAWPILE is Characters, which I have consistently rated 9/10 as the characters are so well crafted. The Atmosphere, Writing, Logic and Enjoyment all came out at a 7 this time, so again not bad, but not fantastic. Plot and Intrigue both came out at a 6, which is where I am most let down. <br /><br />This really felt like a book of two halves for me. The first half of this book was a total bore to me, and had me wanting to DNF it. I felt like the plot was going around in circles, and each time the same cycle happened, I found myself caring less and less for it. It was only around the 400 page park that the plot picked up and it felt like we were actually moving forward with anything. From that point on it was a much more fast-paced story and my intrigue was back up again. But 400 pages in... I don't think that was enough for me to rating plot and intrigue any higher than a 6. However, I recognise that if we didn't have these 400 pages of 'struggle' then I likely would have said something about how everything was overcome too easily - the struggle was needed, but perhaps only 200 pages of it would have done the job.<br /><br />I, quite honestly, also found the ending to be a little disappointing... I wasn't emotional about any of it at all, but I suppose it was interesting how we got to that point. I enjoyed the unfolding of information and seeing the revelations, I just wish I was more emotionally attached to it.<br /><br />I do believe that my favourite thing about Robin Hobb's books is her female characters - I find them the most compelling and interesting characters to read about, and do love how boldly they stand out in such a male-dominated genre of its time. I would love to read on more about Ketricken, learn Kettles back story in full, or see the life of Starling Birdsong. <br /><br />That being said, I had a love for Fitz, and oh how I just wished for something good for the boy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4685717426354352245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kaora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7983564-kaora"><img alt="Kaora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542069606p2/7983564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/868927430?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaora" href="/user/show/7983564-kaora">Kaora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553565690" href="/book/show/45112.Assassin_s_Quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7983564-kaora?shelf=good-fantasy-series">good-fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer868927430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2482483144877483583"><i>He shall thirst for the blood of his own kin, and his thirst shall go unslaked. The Catalyst shall hunger for a hearth and children in vain, for his children shall be another's and another's child his own.</i><br/><br/>For approximately 60% of this book I was positive it was going to be 2-3 stars. For such a massive book there didn't seem to be a lot happening. We follow Fitz as he attempts to find himself after dying and being reborn after living as a wolf. It begins very interesting, but soon began to drag </span>
  <span id="freeText2482483144877483583" style="display:none"><i>He shall thirst for the blood of his own kin, and his thirst shall go unslaked. The Catalyst shall hunger for a hearth and children in vain, for his children shall be another's and another's child his own.</i><br /><br />For approximately 60% of this book I was positive it was going to be 2-3 stars. For such a massive book there didn't seem to be a lot happening. We follow Fitz as he attempts to find himself after dying and being reborn after living as a wolf. It begins very interesting, but soon began to drag as each day becomes seemingly mundane details of Fitz' travels, including the smells he encounters and the animals he hunts.<br /><br />However I feel like the last 40% completely changed how I viewed the book. I found myself engrossed, unable to put it down. And books that capture my attention that completely are usually 5 stars. However I can't forgive that slow beginning and middle, so we shall settle for a 4.<br /><br /><i>The only dream I had after that was of a lone wolf, running, endlessly running. He was as alone as I was.</i><br /><br />Fitz is still Fitz. While he is not my favorite character in this series mainly due to his whiny and dramatic nature, I really enjoy how well established every character is, despite my feelings towards them. Take the villain, Regal. I can see why he is the way he is. My favorite characters seem to change from book to book, as I learn more about each one.<br /><br />There was also a number of twists that I did not see coming, but the main thing that kept me riveted was learning about the history of the Six Duchies, the Elderlings and the various forms of magic including Skilling and the Wit. There is an amazing world created in these books and I just love to explore it.<br /><br />Well... For the most part.<br /><br />Cross posted at <a href="http://www.hisaye.net/assassins-quest-robin-hobb/" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaora's Corner</a>.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_831566438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/831566438" />
    <a title="Damian Dubois" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481936-damian-dubois"><img alt="Damian Dubois" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594640113p2/3481936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/831566438?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Damian Dubois" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Damian Dubois" href="/user/show/3481936-damian-dubois">Damian Dubois</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006480112" href="/book/show/68493.Assassin_s_Quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3481936-damian-dubois?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer831566438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8405639739349591365">Just as a friendly word of warning this review contains many spoilers that haven’t been wrapped in spoiler tags so I would recommend only reading this review if you have already completed the Farseer Trilogy. Wouldn’t want to ruin things for you…<br/><br/>At the end of <i>Royal Assassin</i> we were left on a cliffhanger which saw Chade and Burrich engaging in a little spot of grave robbing, an exhumation of sorts to reunite Fitz’s soul with something that sets Nighteyes hackles ajar, something he describes as sm</span>
  <span id="freeText8405639739349591365" style="display:none">Just as a friendly word of warning this review contains many spoilers that haven’t been wrapped in spoiler tags so I would recommend only reading this review if you have already completed the Farseer Trilogy. Wouldn’t want to ruin things for you…<br /><br />At the end of <i>Royal Assassin</i> we were left on a cliffhanger which saw Chade and Burrich engaging in a little spot of grave robbing, an exhumation of sorts to reunite Fitz’s soul with something that sets Nighteyes hackles ajar, something he describes as smelling like spoilt meat. Burrich wins the battle of wits and wrestles Fitz’s soul back into his body – queue thunder, a bit of lightning and Burrich looking to the heavens and shouting, “He’s alive, by Eda, he’s alive!”<br /><br />Fitz, once again reunited with his battered and bruised body courtesy of the wonderfully friendly soldiers in the employ of one Prince Regal, grudgingly submits himself to a period of rehabilitation, to learn once more the manners of a royal bastard instead of tearing meat from the bone and lapping up water from the nearest stream like his fluffy companion, Nighteyes. Time progresses and once Fitz realises that death has released him from his bond to the late King Shrewd, Fitz decides that for once he is going to do something that he has longed to do – something that I have myself longed for him to do – and that is to play the part of the Royal Assassin and dial up regicide and reap bloody vengeance on the self proclaimed, King Regal.<br /><br />Now, knowing who we are dealing with here, Fitz botches the assignment (yes, I am harsh, his plans never seem to go as planned) but manages to escape with a little help from the real King, Verity, but in the process receives a new set of orders via the Skill to ‘Come to me’. Fitz finds that no matter what he wants to do he is compelled to seek out Verity, wherever he may be (Verity gave him the command, but not the location – and yes, sounds mad but he does have his reasons for being vague).<br /><br />And thus begins our <i>Assassin’s Quest</i> where Fitz does just what a quest entails. He travels. And travels. And boy does he travel. He spends time as a shepherd whilst with a troupe of puppeteers and is sold out to Regal’s guards. He spends some quality time with some pilgrims being smuggled all the way to the mountain kingdom of Jhaampe and, you guessed it, is sold out to Regal’s guards – see the pattern developing here? ;) He hooks up with a minstrel, Starling, a lovely young lass that is enamoured with Fitz – not with him per se, but because of the events that surround him. Catalyst. Changer. He also manages to make it into Jhaampe where he is then reunited with his Queen, Kettricken, and the irrepressibly lovable Fool. Fitz even comes across his very own yellow brick road (the road that Skill built) and Sculptures by the Sea (the forest of the Elderlings).<br /><br />But enough of Fitz’s travels. Robin Hobb for me is one of the better authors I know when it comes to characterisation – in fact you’ll probably find in all of my reviews of Robin Hobb’s books that they are full of praise for this particular aspect of her writing. <i>Assassin’s Quest</i> is no exception. There are just so many great characters here on display whether it be the Fool or Fitz or Chade or Molly or Burrich or Nighteyes… you get the picture. There are two characters I would like to say a few words about – one that seems to be much maligned, the other much loved.<br /><br /><b>Molly</b>. I like Molly and can’t really understand the reason for others not liking her or thinking that Fitz’s heart doesn’t really beat for her (My heart beats for another!) or even that Hobb wasn’t committed to this particular relationship. Molly absolutely loved Fitz and wanted a life together with him. Fitz wanted nothing more than to be with her but was a victim of circumstance due to him being born a royal bastard and thus becoming a pawn in the Farseer’s version of a Game of Thrones. Even after his ‘death’ he still couldn’t return to Molly due to the Skill command issued by Verity and the fact she thought he had been killed by Regal in his dungeons. Their relationship was definitely a victim of circumstance. I also absolutely felt for Fitz when he found out that he had a daughter and that the only way he could ever see her was through his wayward dreaming via the Skill. Sad indeed.<br /><br /><b>The Fool</b>. I’ll just throw my <i>Ancillary Justice</i> reference in here and maybe, just like Breq, stick to the female gender pronoun when discussing the Fool ;) Wouldn’t that make some people I know seriously unhappy if the Fool turned out to be female, haha. Whatever the actual gender of our albino-turned-amber prophet, the Fool in this novel gets a lot more screen time with more background details released on life before meeting up with our beloved Fitzy-Fitz. The Fool is one character that has it all – wit, pathos, a wicked sense of honour and a kind and benevolent soul. Definitely a remarkable and memorable character.<br /><br />The ending seems to also have divided popular opinion as well with the book practically being wound up in the very last chapter. While I would liked to have read a little more on how the Six Duchies was won back from the sustained threat of the Red Ship Raiders, I acknowledge that this trilogy was Fitz’s tale all along and that the Red Ship threat was only secondary to this. It was cool to also find out the secret behind the ‘Forging’ technique employed by the Outislanders on the folk of the Six Duchies although I’m still not sure how they were able to store the forged folk’s feelings and emotion within the shining black stone contained in the hulls of their White Ships.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Circles and circles, as the Fool once told me. The Outislanders raided our shore, so King Wisdom brought the Elderlings to drive them back. And the Elderlings Forged the Outislanders with Skill when they flew over their huts so frequently. Generations later, they came to raid our shores and Forge our folk. So King Verity went to wake the Elderlings, and the Elderlings drove them back. And Forged them in the process. I wonder if once more the hate will fester until…</i>
</blockquote><br />This was my second time through the Farseer Trilogy but due to that first read being over a decade ago it actually felt like a new book to me. I knew the basic outline of the story and remembered some of the key moments but it was only during my reading when my memories of some of the finer details were tickled awake and came to the surface.<br /><br />So, three down and another ten to go until I can safely read <i>The Fool’s Assassin</i> when that is released later this year.<br /><br />5 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8405639739349591365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link831566438" title="Flag this review as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=831566438&amp;resource_type=Review&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F33396914-assassin-s-quest">flag</a>





      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_831566438'><a id="like_count_review_831566438" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/831566438?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">39 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F33396914-assassin-s-quest">Like</a></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3079362362" />
    <a title="Gary " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27528763-gary"><img alt="Gary " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499717454p2/27528763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3079362362?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary " href="/user/show/27528763-gary">Gary </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27528763-gary?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27528763-gary?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3079362362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10113372710580124499">Once again this is more of a rating than a review. I plan to go back and update this with more details later.<br/>I read all of the negative reviews after I finished and I am glad I didn’t read them first. I liked it and thought that the author finished the series well- it was satisfying. The villain could’ve been more developed, but I thought everything tied up nicely. Yes, Fitzgerald was weak, but that was part of what made him a different protagonist than the typical fantasy genre hero. He was cap</span>
  <span id="freeText10113372710580124499" style="display:none">Once again this is more of a rating than a review. I plan to go back and update this with more details later.<br />I read all of the negative reviews after I finished and I am glad I didn’t read them first. I liked it and thought that the author finished the series well- it was satisfying. The villain could’ve been more developed, but I thought everything tied up nicely. Yes, Fitzgerald was weak, but that was part of what made him a different protagonist than the typical fantasy genre hero. He was capable of killing a lot of people, but needed constant help. Emotionally he was always on edge, which kept me on edge. A large part of the story involves traveling from one location to another, which prevents the thorough development of a setting until near the end. This can put some readers off, and I typically am not a fan of this type of structure, but it works in this story.<br />I have this a five star rating because I liked the characters and I enjoy a tightly plotted novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10113372710580124499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2798345444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2798345444" />
    <a title="Anish Kohli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli"><img alt="Anish Kohli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579696384p2/20963257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2798345444?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anish Kohli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anish Kohli" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli">Anish Kohli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6352143-assassin-s-quest">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20963257-anish-kohli?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2798345444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3400430430450600258"><b>
  <blockquote>“The separation from those who had cared about me was more than I could bear. Had I been truly a wolf, I would have lifted my nose to the sky and howled.”</blockquote>
</b> Alrighty! Let’s make a rule. Going forward, for all Robin Hobb reads, my reviews will begin with a small cussing section aimed at Hobb. No, it’s not bcz of anything she did wrong. It’s just bcz how much she makes Fitz suffer. And how much of a cruel author she is. So with that decided, let’s begin!<br/><br/>DAMN YOU, ROBIN HOBB!! What in hell posses</span>
  <span id="freeText3400430430450600258" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“The separation from those who had cared about me was more than I could bear. Had I been truly a wolf, I would have lifted my nose to the sky and howled.”</blockquote>
</b> Alrighty! Let’s make a rule. Going forward, for all Robin Hobb reads, my reviews will begin with a small cussing section aimed at Hobb. No, it’s not bcz of anything she did wrong. It’s just bcz how much she makes Fitz suffer. And how much of a cruel author she is. So with that decided, let’s begin!<br /><br />DAMN YOU, ROBIN HOBB!! What in hell possessed you to write so cruelly? What came over you to put Fitz through so much? Did he ever do you wrong? Did he steal from you? How could he, he’s FICTIONAL! So why the hell do you hate that boy so damn much? Just why? Dammit all to hell, Hobb. You broke my heart! But I love you so we’re kinda good.<br /><br />There, I feel so much better having gotten that out of my system. I have really enjoyed this book and the series on the whole. I can say that hands down, this is one of the best fantasy series I have read so far. Surely this is far slower than the average book we will read and in terms of marked big events it is lacking but the execution is done so well that I couldn’t help but love it. BUT, I’m getting ahead of myself. I’ll detail these things later in my review. <br />Without much more incoherent babbling/gushing, let me dive right into the more structured review. I’m not gonna be talking about the plot bcz it’s hard to do that and not give out spoilers so yeah….<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Writing</b>
</u><br />Gosh dang, it is great. I said the same thing in my last two reviews as well. I have personally always preferred the 3rd person POV and most of the times 1st person POV doesn’t work for me even remotely. But the way Hobb writes, I can totally get behind this kinda 1st person POV. It is amazingly well done and the flow is so smooth that I never once felt any sort of a hiccup while reading. It is so compulsive, the story is woven so nicely, that it kept pulling me back to it and I kept reading the book even at work. It had a complete hold on me. And I thoroughly enjoyed it. <br /><br />There is this section of the book about Fitz going on a quest with a few others on the Skill road to find Verity and man, that section of the book is so trippy! I was reading it and I was like am I high or is this book making me feel like I am high and nothing is making complete sense. Jokes aside though, that part was so damn well executed bcz it needed to read like it was trippy and as if the senses of a person were stunted in some way and Hobb got that so spot on! That section has to be a highlight for me in this book!<br /><br />But I guess, in my opinion, the real mark of an author is when they can make you see an established thing in a completely different light. Hobb achieved that through Chade when he is parting his way with Fitz and how he makes the reader realize that Fitz isn’t all that blameless in all this mess. How Fitz, while always thinking he is obeying them all, went about doing things that he was advised against, regardless. I loved this bit. I guess on the writing front I am all praises so we’ll be moving on.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Characters</b>
</u><br />For this book the cast is pretty trimmed down but not lean by any measure. There were a couple of new additions to the cast and I think they were just as fab. Let’s talk about them and select few of the main cast.<br /><br />&gt;&gt; Kettle <i>
  <blockquote>“This cannot be right. It simply cannot be right. The Prophet and the Catalyst, and you are scarcely more than boys. Green to manhood, untrained in Skill, full of pranks and lovesick woes. These are the ones sent to save the world?”</blockquote>
</i> Oh I really enjoyed her character. She was snarky and pretty much a decent addition. She added a certain charm to the story for me. Although I don’t see why she couldn’t reveal all her secrets, even when the time came or why she couldn’t help Fitz. <br /><br />&gt;&gt; Starling <i>
  <blockquote>“I learned long ago not to blame myself for evil done to me. It wasn’t my fault. It wasn’t even your fault. You were just the catalyst that started the chain of events.”</blockquote>
</i> Well, not sure if I really liked her or not. She was a character whose motivations were never clear to me, not by much. Sure it was stated clearly why she was doing what she did but I didn’t really hit home for me. Overall I think she was done pretty well as a side character.<br /><br />&gt;&gt; Verity <i>
  <blockquote>“I did love you, you know,” he said brusquely. “Despite all I’ve done to you, I loved you.”</blockquote>
</i> Ah Verity! My heart broke for him all this while when he was gone and it broke even more when we found him to see what’s become of him. But like I said in the review of previous book, Verity is a highly resilient character and I like him for that. He’s always had a singlemindedness about him that is both, his boon and bane. I also liked the dynamics he shared with Fitz. And although he could have done much better by him, I think he did the best he could do it as a person he was. <br /><br />&gt;&gt; Fool <i>
  <blockquote>“Tomorrow comes early. And we’ve work to do.” He laughed unevenly. “We’ve the world to save, you and I”</blockquote>
</i> Hands down THE MOST enigmatic character I have ever read! Even when there is so much revealed about him, I feel like we barely know the Fool but then again, we do know him. He adds sass and life to this book in his own way. I really love the character and want more of him. I think I want a book, atleast partially from the Fool’s perspective. Do we get that later into the series?<br /><br />&gt;&gt; Nighteyes <i>
  <blockquote>“Wolves have no Kings!”</blockquote>
</i> This quote hits home for me, for some reason. And I think it will stay with me for a long time. I think, the beauty of this character lies in the fact that through Nighteyes, Hobb could say things in a bare naked way that most human character will not be able to convey without coming across as crass or unlikeable. I love how he is shaped as a companion to Fitz and not as a pet. I absolutely love how he defies Fitz and does what he feels like, regardless. The dynamic between Fitz &amp; Nighteyes is so good that I can’t explain. I want more of them!<br /><br />&gt;&gt; FitzChivalry <i>
  <blockquote>“If I had nothing else out of this crust of life Burrich and Chade had salvaged for me, I would have revenge.”</blockquote>
</i> Hands down, never seen a character suffer more than Fitz. Ever. And I think it is this very reason that the series works so well. Fitz stuck in this life, neither wanting to play the game nor able to get rid of it. Neither does he want to be controlled nor can he seize control. Fitz gave a hell of a lot more than he ever gained from the bargain he struck with King Shrewd. I think he paid for it dearly. Yes, Fitz was stupid in many many occasions but you have to remember he is just a young boy, not a man, no matter what these princes put on him or how they trained him. Gosh my heart hurts that Hobb put Fitz through so much and never ever gave him a chance to come out on top. Fitz, my boy, you are one of the dearest characters I have read. You are a star! <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Magic System</b>
</u><br />Again, I had the same complaint as the last time. The Magic system is pretty open ended. The limits of skill, the usage of it and the Wit are just not defined well enough. If I am to be completely honest with myself, I think it serves more as a plot convenience. Fitz gets saved multiple times due to this open ended system. Towards the end Hobb did expand on it vastly and used it far more than she did in any other book so far but that makes it even more irksome to me. What is the Skill based in, how is it now a physical thing than an abstract thing, how is it being used to craft things? It is all too ambiguous. Although the enjoyment value is great but if I am as critical with this book as I am with others, then this part needs major development.<br />I wish for a better defined Magic system with hard rules and repercussions of pushing those rules. I think Hobb has the capacity to do that and the fact that she didn’t makes me all the more disappointed. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Problem Areas</b>
</u><br />With this book, I have many problems. They might sound small on surface but considering how well done this series has been, they are pretty huge complaints. <br /><br />&gt;&gt; I found it ludicrous that suddenly, and in the span of such a short time, atleast three (maybe four?) girls quite literally throw themselves at Fitz, wanting to be bed by him. Sure, the reasons for one out of three were made clear but the other two just wanted to sleep with him. Why? And why now? It’s not like Fitz is the most handsome guy or something. Even if he had been, it would still not be as plausible to me. It irked me, to say the least. <br /><br />&gt;&gt; I am absolutely not a fan of the fact how late Hobb resolved the conflicts of the series. I mean this book is a conclusion to a trilogy and till about 92% mark, everyone is still in danger with no solution in sight but within the span of less than 5% of the remaining book, everything was resolved and I do not appreciate it. I do have an inkling that this ending might link upto things in the next books but even so I kinda wanted a bit better wrap up.<br /><br />&gt;&gt; My biggest issue is this: All through the series, Fitz uses the Skill intermittently. His Skill capability was ruined by Galen in the first book itself but despite that he can Skill quite a bit and especially in some occasions it is not the small or accidental Skilling but the more practiced kind and that annoys me. It’s like he has just the right amount of capability left to further the plot. <br /><br />&gt;&gt; My previous issue bleeds into this one and thus making this close to a plot hole for me. Fitz cures Kettle whose Skill was burned centuries ago by Skilling to her, which he shouldn’t be able to do in the first place but that’s not my problem. My problem is that when Kettle could be cured, why the fuck is no one doing it for Fitz? What went so wrong with his Skill that it can never be put right? I needed more details on this front. It’s like no one, Verity included, even wanted to understand how Galen ruined Fitz’s Skilling and ever try to put it right. <br /><br />&gt;&gt; This one is a complaint out of pettiness, and yes, I am being petty bcz God dammit I hated how Hobb made us wait for 3 whole books just to give a glimpse of Dragons and then she shuts shop with such a short cameo! Woman, you need to understand that Dragons are fucking important and that you can never have enough of them! Bring them back now, Hobb!! <br />Alright, alright, this point doesn’t count as a problem area but please, more Dragons, pleaseeee? <br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Overall Impact</b>
</u><br />There are so many things I loved in this book and so many I didn’t care much for. I was absolutely a fan of the way things were wrapped up with Regal! I just totally loved that! It was so satisfying that it let out a great sigh of relief and did a fist pump followed by a “Yes!” I think in terms of Regal, no other end could have been better.<br />The story arc with Molly &amp; Burrich, I saw it coming through book 2 itself but I think that that was a thing that made sense even if wasn’t what we wanted and it broke my heart to see Fitz at that point of time. <br />Most of the things were fine but the ending was lackluster for me and it seemed kinda rushed. I also wasn’t a fan of the fact how Chade was just sidelined completely from the ending. <br /><br />I think, all said and done, this is one of the best series I have read in terms of writing and world building. Surely the fantasy elements left me wanting for more but then again, I got such amazing characters that I am not scared anymore when I think that I have a long journey left in the Realm of Elderlings. I look forward to it and I hope to see these characters soon. <b>
  <blockquote>“Perhaps there can be no thanks nor any blame, but only recognition of the forces that brought us and bound us to our inevitable fates.”</blockquote>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3400430430450600258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3008921095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3008921095" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3008921095?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=favourites-2020">favourites-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2020-tbr-challenge">2020-tbr-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3008921095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6011359554234018716">So, notwithstanding all the travelling, which I know some people find tedious to read, I loved this book. I think reading the Farseer Trilogy books in succession was definitely the way to go, as all 2000 or so pages really do sit firmly in my mind as a single tale.<br/><br/>Some (but definitely not all) favourite things from this final book:<br/><br/>*Hobbs' treatment of PTSD and residual trauma. Wow, just so excellently done, not just for Fitz, but Kettricken, and all the characters who suffered so in the making o</span>
  <span id="freeText6011359554234018716" style="display:none">So, notwithstanding all the travelling, which I know some people find tedious to read, I loved this book. I think reading the Farseer Trilogy books in succession was definitely the way to go, as all 2000 or so pages really do sit firmly in my mind as a single tale.<br /><br />Some (but definitely not all) favourite things from this final book:<br /><br />*Hobbs' treatment of PTSD and residual trauma. Wow, just so excellently done, not just for Fitz, but Kettricken, and all the characters who suffered so in the making of this story.<br /><br />*The relationship between Nighteyes and Fitz is an obvious highlight, and I love how it grows and changes. Nighteyes and his burgeoning personhood, as well as his growing relationships with others of his found family/pack was also a standout element for me.<br /><br />*The dragons! Ok, these were truly awesome. Their emergence was harrowing, emotional, and had me trying to decide whether I was pleased or horrified (both, really).<br /><br />Again Hobbs shows what a master she is at characterisation. If I have one complaint, it might be that Regal, while absolutely and truly horrible, is not quite as complicated as I might like. That's a minor complaint though in a huge cast of exceptionally well rendered players.<br /><br />Overall just so excellent. As a whole, the Farseer Trilogy ranks among my all time favourites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6011359554234018716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165256-penny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400023048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17349732799614809036">After re-read:<br/>As I said the first time I read this book, the first third of this book was not great. However it was more than worth slogging through it for the rest of the book which I really enjoyed. If you're worried about starting a huge series of 16 books, don't be. I'd have been perfectly content to leave this where it ends. It's a nicely contained trilogy that doesn't require the later books in the series for you to feel it was complete. <br/><br/>That said, I'm already on to the next trilogy that F</span>
  <span id="freeText17349732799614809036" style="display:none">After re-read:<br />As I said the first time I read this book, the first third of this book was not great. However it was more than worth slogging through it for the rest of the book which I really enjoyed. If you're worried about starting a huge series of 16 books, don't be. I'd have been perfectly content to leave this where it ends. It's a nicely contained trilogy that doesn't require the later books in the series for you to feel it was complete. <br /><br />That said, I'm already on to the next trilogy that Fitz is in (skipping the Liveship Traders books for now even though I really enjoyed those the first time I read them. I can't leave Fitz for that long.)<br /><br />First review:<br />I didn't particularly enjoy the first third of this book but I loved the rest. The last in a trilogy is usually my favourite since it contains the answers to those questions that have been building up throughout the series. This was my first time reading Robin Hobb and I'm a fan! A highly enjoyable wonderful series!</span>
